<p itemprop="description">
Nineteen-year-old Alice returns to the magical world from her childhood adventure, where she reunites with her old friends and learns of her true destiny: to end the Red Queen's reign of terror.</p>

        <h2>Storyline</h2>
        
        <div class="inline canwrap" itemprop="description">
            <p>
Alice, an unpretentious and individual 19-year-old, is betrothed to a dunce of an English nobleman. At her engagement party, she escapes the crowd to consider whether to go through with the marriage and falls down a hole in the garden after spotting an unusual rabbit. Arriving in a strange and surreal place called "Underland," she finds herself in a world that resembles the nightmares she had as a child, filled with talking animals, villainous queens and knights, and frumious bandersnatches. Alice realizes that she is there for a reason--to conquer the horrific Jabberwocky and restore the rightful queen to her throne.                <em class="nobr">Written by
<a href="/search/title?plot_author=Jim Beaver <jumblejim@prodigy.net>&view=simple&sort=alpha"
>Jim Beaver &lt;jumblejim@prodigy.net&gt;</a></em>            </p>
        </div>
        
        <span class="see-more inline"> 
                <a href="/title/tt1014759/plotsummary?ref_=tt_stry_pl"
>Plot Summary</a>
    <span>|</span>

        <h2>Did You Know?</h2>
    <div id="trivia" class="txt-block">
        <h4>Trivia</h4>


Final film of <a href="/name/nm0001284?ref_=tt_trv_trv">Michael Gough</a>, who had previously worked in four other <a href="/name/nm0000318?ref_=tt_trv_trv">Tim Burton</a> movies.        <a href="trivia?ref_=tt_trv_trv"
class="nobr" >See more</a>  &raquo;
    </div>
                <hr />
     <div id="goofs"  class="txt-block">
        <h4>Goofs</h4>
While riding the Bandersnatch to the White Queen's castle, Alice meets Bayard and asks him to guide her to Marmoreal even though the castle's name was never mentioned in the movie before.        <a href="trivia?tab=gf&ref_=tt_trv_gf"
class="nobr" >See more</a>  &raquo;
    </div>   
                <hr />
    <div id="quotes" class="text-block">
        <h4>Quotes</h4>
[<span class="fine">first lines</span>]
<br /><a href="/name/nm0683116/?ref_=tt_trv_qu"

Charles, you have lost your senses? This picture is impossible.
<br /><a href="/name/nm0190744/?ref_=tt_trv_qu"

Precisely. Gentlemen, the only way to achieve the impossible, is to believe it's possible.

class="nobr" >See more</a> &raquo;
    </div>
                <hr />
     <div id="crazyCredits"  class="txt-block">
        <h4>Crazy Credits</h4>
The ending credits have flowers going from dead to blooming, a sun rising and setting, and vines moving around.        <a href="trivia?tab=cz&ref_=tt_trv_cc"
class="nobr" >See more</a>  &raquo;
    </div>

    <div class="article" id="titleUserReviewsTeaser">
        <h2>User Reviews</h2>
        <div class="user-comments">
                    <div class="tinystarbar" title="5/10">
                        <div style="width: 50px;">&nbsp;</div>
                    </div>
                <span itemprop="review" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">  
                    <strong itemprop="name">some stunning visuals, clumsy writing</strong>
                    <span itemprop="reviewRating" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Rating">
                        <meta itemprop="worstRating" content = "1" />
                        <meta itemprop="ratingValue" content="5" />
                        <meta itemprop="bestRating" content="10" />
                    </span>
                    <div class="comment-meta">
                        5 March 2010 | by <a href="/user/ur15710816/?ref_=tt_urv"
><span itemprop="author">ericpendley</span></a>
                        <meta itemprop="datePublished" content="2010-03-05" />
                              (Austin, TX, United States)
                        &ndash; <a href="/user/ur15710816/comments?ref_=tt_urv"
>See all my reviews</a>
                    </div>
                    <div>
                        <p itemprop="reviewBody">It is still worth the high price of the 3-D admission to see some of the amazing animation and design, but the writing is extremely boring and clumsy, and the performances cannot save it. Too many liberties were taken with the originals here, and in no way improve upon them, it only barely resembles either of Carroll&#x27;s books in theme and some specific scenes. There are some &#x22;Disney moments&#x22; that literally set off a gag reflex as well.<br /><br />The animation is quite stunning and wonderful though, as is the costuming and set design (in so much as there were sets and not just green screens, I&#x27;m sure SOME actual props were used). There are some clever elements that owe only to good visual design and direction I&#x27;m sure, as the only other clever bits in the dialogue were the parts directly lifted from the originals.</p>
                    </div>
                </span>
                <hr />
                <div class="yn" id="ynd_2216471">
                    288 of 442 people found this review helpful.&nbsp;

                    <button class="btn small" value="No" name="ynb_2216471_no" onclick="CS.TMD.user_review_vote(2216471, 'tt1014759', 'no');" >No</button>
                </div>
